  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492382680" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10292783-rolyn" class="left imgcol" title="Rolyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372120127p2/10292783.jpg" alt="Rolyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/492382680?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10292783-rolyn" class="user" title="Rolyn">Rolyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119389.Windmills_of_the_Gods" title="Paperback 9780006174424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer492382680">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14611379948084711972">It could have been 5 stars but I found the beginning somewhat slow-paced. But the story, as a whole, was good.<br /><br />I would like to talk about some of the characters...<br /><br /><strong>Edward.</strong> What happened to him was heartbreaking. An innocent party that took the "fall" for the benefit of others.<br /><br /><strong>Groza.</strong> Below was what happened to him/his family...<br /><em>"Scenes of his wife and his daughter being raped seared through his brain. It was a gang rape, and the laughing soldiers went from the woman to the child, their pants pulled</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14611379948084711972">It could have been 5 stars but I found the beginning somewhat slow-paced. But the story, as a whole, was good.<br /><br />I would like to talk about some of the characters...<br /><br /><strong>Edward.</strong> What happened to him was heartbreaking. An innocent party that took the "fall" for the benefit of others.<br /><br /><strong>Groza.</strong> Below was what happened to him/his family...<br /><em>"Scenes of his wife and his daughter being raped seared through his brain. It was a gang rape, and the laughing soldiers went from the woman to the child, their pants pulled down, waiting in line for their turn. Marin Groza strained against the stool as though bound to it. As the whip fell again and again he could hear the screams of his wife and daughter begging for mercy, choking on the men’s<br />penises in their mouths, being raped and sodomized at the same time, until the blood started pouring out and their cries finally trailed off."</em><br /><br /><img width="300" height="169" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/273240.gif" /><br /><br /><strong>Harry Lantz.</strong> If I remembered it correctly, he was the one having threesome. Well, at least he enjoyed his sex life before he forced himself to bed Nuesca. The distance he would go for money would have been funny if not pathetic. Too bad he wasn't as clever as he thought he was.<br /><br /><strong>Mary Ashley.</strong> She proved her worth. Excelled in a place dominated by <em>"male chauvinist pigs".</em> Knows how to play dirty and turn a situation to her benefit. Smart woman. Smart woman until she fell in love. Falling in love was her downfall. Wait. Let me amend that. Falling in love <strong>WITH THE WRONG MAN</strong> was her downfall. If she intended to trust no one, then she shouldn't make an exception. Emotions cloud judgment. She made herself believe all the things Louis said just because she thought he loves her. What a joke. Sabi nga nung lola ko nung nabubuhay pa sya, <em>"Walang ikalawang glorya".</em> And in this case, I agree with her.<br /><br /><strong>Louis, Mike Slade</strong> and <strong>Stanton.</strong> I am happy with myself. I know this is just a book. That they are just fictional characters but I was freaking glad that I pegged all three of them correctly. Even if what I was reading at a certain moment contradicted with what I thought their characters were, I stood by my assumptions. For <strong>Louis</strong>, <img width="500" height="268" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403076r/783998._SX540_SY540_.gif" /><br />For <strong>Mike Slade</strong>, <img width="500" height="281" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380403076r/783999._SX540_SY540_.gif" /><br />And for you, <strong>Stanton</strong>, <img width="500" height="212" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376143ra/730902.gif" /><br /><br />All in all, I really, really, REALLY liked it.<br /><br />Oh! I forgot someone. <strong>Ben Cohn</strong>. The ever adorable Ben Cohn. Who the hell name their penis ARTHUR? Why Arthur out of all names? Or, in the first place, why name his penis? He was weird. Too nosy for his own good. And as they say, <em>curiosity killed the cat</em>.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7570949981230419742">I think I just forgot how to spell the word OSM (as in the impression saying how you were extremely impressed and inspired with great admiration to something, apprehension/ def: extremely good; excellent) because this book is more than just OSM. *crying, tears of joy* lol. :))<br /><br />Anyway, setting that emotion and the feeling that my <em>mind-has-been-"Sheldonized"</em> aside (hahaha). Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel written by my all-time favorite American writer (shall I say his name uh-gain?</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7570949981230419742">I think I just forgot how to spell the word OSM (as in the impression saying how you were extremely impressed and inspired with great admiration to something, apprehension/ def: extremely good; excellent) because this book is more than just OSM. *crying, tears of joy* lol. :))<br /><br />Anyway, setting that emotion and the feeling that my <em>mind-has-been-"Sheldonized"</em> aside (hahaha). Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel written by my all-time favorite American writer (shall I say his name uh-gain? yep! Sidney Sheldon). I think Sheldon defied the laws approvingly in writing this book! Hoho. It’s a story about the world where Iron Curtain still exists (overtly, of course ;). Back from the end of World War II in 1945 until the end of the Cold War in 1991, Iron Curtain was utilized to separate the ideological conflict and physical boundary dividing Europe, hence, the democratic sphere and the communist sphere was thoroughly divided. Windmills of the Gods, on the other hand, is a story under the "Iron Curtain days" where the utmost concern of the United States to Eastern Europe bloc (particularly in Romania) was fictionally discussed. And damn it was overly intriguing, heart-thrilling and mind-boggling!<br /><br />The first situation that appealed me is when Sheldon introduced a beautiful and accomplished scholar who has suddenly became the newest United States ambassador to an Iron Curtain country, a woman who is about to dramatically change the course of world events. Imagine how her pretty face could survive on the glinting edge of East-West confrontation. <br /><br />Every chapter is exceptionally impressive. Exceptionally and excessively impressive. <br /><br />This novel grabbed me with all its all-sort of cliff-hangers, hooks and everything that come with it and finished read it in just one-sitting. RECOMMENDED!!! *__*</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152885201">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3879746033920308404">How a story is presented in the beginning, middle, &amp; end is an essential factor that keeps the readers of into pages. Sidney Sheldon did it well on his Windmills of the Gods, &amp; successfully placed a strong ingredient that surprises readers every now &amp; then. The pacing is perfect. The plot is excellent. The story itself is well-researched. Windmills of the Gods is one of the greatest suspense stories I've had read, and Sidney Sheldon succeeded in hooking me up with such a breath-takin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3879746033920308404">How a story is presented in the beginning, middle, &amp; end is an essential factor that keeps the readers of into pages. Sidney Sheldon did it well on his Windmills of the Gods, &amp; successfully placed a strong ingredient that surprises readers every now &amp; then. The pacing is perfect. The plot is excellent. The story itself is well-researched. Windmills of the Gods is one of the greatest suspense stories I've had read, and Sidney Sheldon succeeded in hooking me up with such a breath-taking story, a fast-paced journey unto the world of politics &amp; its darkest mysteries, the hidden risks behind intellect &amp; fame, the roller coaster ride to the international secrets, sex &amp; murder at their worst, a family at danger in every choice to take, and the survival amidst greedy interests and deceits in a game of life. There's only a few writers who can bring it on; and Sidney Sheldon is one worth to get such prestige.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/37827766-aditya-jain" class="user" title="Aditya Jain">Aditya Jain</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1279770683">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1553618200590389082">The good, old political espionage thriller. The typical Sheldon style. A heroine, Mary Ashley, who is an ingenious personality and who is going to change the scenes around Romania with her power as the American Ambassador. Despite this book being the formulaic portrayal of a political thriller, in which none can be trusted and faith is a stupid term, it certainly gets unpredictable at times. The reason being, the projection of multiple characters as villains.<br />Mary Ashley is supposed to bring chan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1553618200590389082">The good, old political espionage thriller. The typical Sheldon style. A heroine, Mary Ashley, who is an ingenious personality and who is going to change the scenes around Romania with her power as the American Ambassador. Despite this book being the formulaic portrayal of a political thriller, in which none can be trusted and faith is a stupid term, it certainly gets unpredictable at times. The reason being, the projection of multiple characters as villains.<br />Mary Ashley is supposed to bring changes to foreign policies in Romania, but there are people who do not want that to happen. And that is where the danger comes in. Rest is a convoluted piece of clandestine meetings, murders, betrayals, suspicions, love and patriotism.<br />The characters are fine, but none have been done very boldly. The sketches does not endear one to them.<br />All in all, a light read, good for travelling, as I did.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer738836361">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer445952672605919650">Sidney Sheldon's "Windmills of the Gods" is the story of Mary Ashley, a Junction City, Kansas wife, mother, and university professor plucked from obscurity to become the US Ambassador to Romania. Ashley has never left Kansas City and plenty of high-level political figures are (understandably) against the ambassadorship. The appointment of Mary Ashley is questionable and sets the reader up to expect some hefty shenanigans. <br /><br />The beginning of the novel is exciting. Covert meetings are taking place a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText445952672605919650">Sidney Sheldon's "Windmills of the Gods" is the story of Mary Ashley, a Junction City, Kansas wife, mother, and university professor plucked from obscurity to become the US Ambassador to Romania. Ashley has never left Kansas City and plenty of high-level political figures are (understandably) against the ambassadorship. The appointment of Mary Ashley is questionable and sets the reader up to expect some hefty shenanigans. <br /><br />The beginning of the novel is exciting. Covert meetings are taking place and the suspense is already building. Sheldon's description of the Iron Curtain countries in the 80's is detailed and chilling. Mary's initial impression of her new undertaking is well crafted and realistic. However, the swift transition from an inexperienced housewife from a farming state to a global figure accomplishing astonishing feats is a little incredulous. It's also a little predictable, though Sheldon's writing style still creates sufficient intrigue with some nice unexpected twists to keep the reader turning the pages.<br /><br />The suspense tends to overshadow the political aspect as Sheldon places more focus on Ashley's mistrust of her own staff and the belief one of more of them is behind the attempts on her life. In the midst of all the drama is a (questionable) deadly assassin whose true identity remains a mystery (vague to avoid spoilers). The text incorporates several murders and the conclusion is satisfying, though the novel itself never seems to achieve the gritty, heart-stopping level of a political thriller anticipated at the beginning. Perhaps the continual references to Ashley's inexperience in the political arena and her former Middle America background are contributory factors. Overall, it is a well-written and enjoyable read. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="445952672605919650">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1970837340183835267">I read this years ago when I was probably far too young to even read such a book and made the mistake of thinking this would be similar to the version I read in a "Reader's Digest" condensed version (it didn't take me long to figure out how the "Reader's Digest" version got so clean). If I could give this novel zero stars, I would. Granted, the political intrigue is okay though the characters are essentially tropes and, honestly, most of the seasons of the show "24" were more solidly written and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1970837340183835267">I read this years ago when I was probably far too young to even read such a book and made the mistake of thinking this would be similar to the version I read in a "Reader's Digest" condensed version (it didn't take me long to figure out how the "Reader's Digest" version got so clean). If I could give this novel zero stars, I would. Granted, the political intrigue is okay though the characters are essentially tropes and, honestly, most of the seasons of the show "24" were more solidly written and far more interesting than this. Likewise, the sexual content can be a bit much, if not needlessly brutal, at times. Definitely not my cup of tea at all and reads like a sensationalist, tasteless supermarket checkout line novel. I've never consider revisiting this book and was happy to rid my shelf of it years ago.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1416225782">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416225782" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3515571-meta-morfillah" class="left imgcol" title="Meta Morfillah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1269961098p2/3515571.jpg" alt="Meta Morfillah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1416225782?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3515571-meta-morfillah" class="user" title="Meta Morfillah">Meta Morfillah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6666637-kincir-angin-para-dewa" title="Paperback 9794035920" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1416225782">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2515302233847952574">Judul: Kincir angin para dewa<br />Penulis: Sidney sheldon<br />Penerbit: -<br />Dimensi: 252 hlm<br />ISBN: -<br /><br />Ini adalah karya kedua sidney sheldon yang saya baca, dan dua-duanya ebook! Wow... suatu rekor bagi saya yang tak menyukai ebook, karena tak kuat berlama-lama menatap gadget dan radiasinya. Sejujurnya mata saya sakit dan kepala saya migrain menatap laptop beberapa jam demi menuntaskan bacaan. Tetapi sejak berkenalan dengan karya Sidney, saya tak bisa tidur bila belum menuntaskannya. Rasa penasaran akan ending d</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2515302233847952574">Judul: Kincir angin para dewa<br />Penulis: Sidney sheldon<br />Penerbit: -<br />Dimensi: 252 hlm<br />ISBN: -<br /><br />Ini adalah karya kedua sidney sheldon yang saya baca, dan dua-duanya ebook! Wow... suatu rekor bagi saya yang tak menyukai ebook, karena tak kuat berlama-lama menatap gadget dan radiasinya. Sejujurnya mata saya sakit dan kepala saya migrain menatap laptop beberapa jam demi  menuntaskan bacaan. Tetapi sejak berkenalan dengan karya Sidney, saya tak bisa tidur bila belum menuntaskannya. Rasa penasaran akan ending dan alur yang begitu memikat membuat saya terjaga terus.<br /><br />Kali ini, di Kincir angin para dewa, sidney mengangkat kisah tentang seorang ibu rumah tangga beranak dua yang hidup sederhana di kansas, yang pada suatu hari mengalami momentum terbesar dalam hidupnya. Mary Ashley--nama perempuan itu--ditawari langsung oleh Presiden Amerika Serikat, Paul Elisson, untuk menjadi duta besar di Rumania. Hal itu bermula dari tulisannya di sebuah koran yang membahas pemikiran politiknya terhadap negara uni soviet dan satelitnya. Hal sederhana yang menurutnya biasa saja, karena memang ia mengajar mata kuliah politik timur dan kakeknya adalah orang rumania--meski ia belum pernah sekali pun keluar dari kansas. Ternyata keputusan presiden begitu mengusik beberapa penguasa. Sehingga terbentuklah organisasi rahasia bernama Politic of freedom--dengan seorang pengawas yang begitu berkuasa dan tak diketahui jati dirinya--yang berniat membunuh Mary dan keluarganya.<br /><br />Hal itu dimulai dengan kematian suaminya, yang dibuat seperti kecelakaan. Keputusan awal Mary yang menolak jabatan duta besar rumania, kini berganti semenjak kematian Edward. Bersama Mike Slade--bawahannya yang bersikap cuek namun perhatian dengan kedua anaknya, Tim &amp; Beth--Mary menjalankan tugasnya di Rumania. Namun nyawanya semakin bahaya, sebab organisasi rahasia itu sudah menyewa pembunuh profesional bernama Angel. Mary frustasi. Beruntunglah, ia mengenal Dr. Louis dari Prancis yang perangainya mirip dengan Edward dan seketika membuatnya jatuh cinta. Tapi ternyata hal itu tak berlangsung lama, hingga ia diracuni suatu hari. Ditambah tekanan bahwa ada kebocoran besar dalam kedutaan. Nyawanya dan anak-anaknya kian terancam, dan kini ia tak bisa memercayai siapa pun.<br /><br />Bisakah Mary menunaikan tugasnya dengan baik? Siapa sebenarnya Sang Pengawas, Angel, dan orang-orang yang terlibat dalam organisasi rahasia tersebut? <br /><br />Dari dua karya ini, saya sudah mulai menebak kecenderungan gaya menulis Sidney dan endingnya. Sidney selalu membuat perbandingan mencolok antara tokoh protagonis dan antagonisnya, dan selaku saja tokoh utama dibuat terkecoh--sama seperti pembaca. Tak lupa isu tentang kelainan seks, dalam buku ini mengenai sadomasochism. Selalu berhasil membuat kaget dengan twist yang tak terduga--meski sebenarnya secara halus Sidney sudah mengirimkan sinyal, namun di kali lain, ia mematahkan sendiri dengan pemikiran tokoh utama, lalu kembali lagi ke premis utama. Alur yang digunakan kali ini cenderung progresif dan terus menciptakan ketegangan, konflik dengan klimaks dan antiklimaks yang berimbang. <br /><br />Mengenai typo, saya menemukan beberapa, entah karena kesalahan teknis karena ini berbentuk ebook pdf, sehingga layoutnya pun berantakan atau karena memang buku aslinya juga typo? Saya tak tahu. Mengenai judulnya sendiri, saya menduga sidney menyimbolkan kekuasaan para penguasa dengan kincir angin para dewa, sebab tema itulah yang diangkat dalam buku ini. Dan Mary seakan domba kurban, mainan para dewa tersebut. Sebagaimana ungkapan pembukanya,<br /><br />"Kita semua adalah korban, Anselmo. Nasib kita ditentukan oleh bergulirnya dadu jagat raya, pengaruh rasi bintang, dan arah angin keberuntungan, yang diembuskan dari kincir angin para dewa." (A final destiny, H. L. Dietrich)<br /><br />Dalam buku ini, saya lebih tertarik dengan gerakan organisasi rahasia yang menggunakan nama dewa sebagai samaran dan strategi pertemuan mereka. Mengingatkan saya pada freemason, persaudaraan, dan iluminati. Untuk kamu yang suka genre kriminal, psikologi, dan detektif, buku ini saya anjurkan untuk dibaca. Lalu, mulailah menebak-nebak siapa pelakunya.<br /><br />Saya apresiasi 4 dari 5 bintang.<br /><br />"Kautahu bagaimana sikap pers. Mereka amat suka melambungkan pahlawan supaya mereka dapat membantingnya jatuh." (Hlm. 10)<br /><br />Meta morfillah</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2515302233847952574">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15114407426088008914">I hadn't read a Sidney Sheldon book in well over a decade. So this was nostalgia on 100. I can honestly say I had forgotten just how enjoyable his novels are. The first time I read any of his novels, it was <a title=" Nothing Lasts Forever" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Nothing%20Lasts%20Forever"> Nothing Lasts Forever</a> and I was 12 years old. I still remember very well how I devoured the pages. He is the master of suspense. This was such a wonderful read that had me gasping in a number of places. The red herring was rather obvious but it didn't matter at all because there were so many</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15114407426088008914">I hadn't read a Sidney Sheldon book in well over a decade. So this was nostalgia on 100. I can honestly say I had forgotten just how enjoyable his novels are. The first time I read any of his novels, it was <a title=" Nothing Lasts Forever" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Nothing%20Lasts%20Forever"> Nothing Lasts Forever</a> and I was 12 years old. I still remember very well how I devoured the pages. He is the master of suspense. This was such a wonderful read that had me gasping in a number of places. The red herring was rather obvious but it didn't matter at all because there were so many plot twists and reveals to keep me happy. Plus he played it out so well that a few times I wasn't as sure of the red herring. Mr. Sheldon truly is the master of suspense.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_722150840">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722150840" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16298000-minky-monster" class="left imgcol" title="minky_monster"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1397790118p2/16298000.jpg" alt="minky_monster" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/722150840?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16298000-minky-monster" class="user" title="minky_monster">minky_monster</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6666637-kincir-angin-para-dewa" title="Paperback 9794035920" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer722150840">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17169427870266934058">Saya udah pernah baca buku Sidney Sheldon ini waktu SMA, pinjem di perpus. Waktu itu mikirnya buku ini ceritanya tentang konspirasi, dan ada bumbu seksnya sedikit. Setelah dibaca lagi, pemahamannya sedikit beda. Memang ada unsur konspirasi, tapi tema utamanya lebih ke arah kisah seorang wanita yg menjadi duta besar.<br /><br />Plot:<br />Buku ini terbit di taun 80an, dimana Perang Dingin masih berlangsung antara Blok Barat dan Timur. Presiden terpilih Amerika, Paul Ellison, ingin mencoba menjalin hubungan baik de</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17169427870266934058">Saya udah pernah baca buku Sidney Sheldon ini waktu SMA, pinjem di perpus. Waktu itu mikirnya buku ini ceritanya tentang konspirasi, dan ada bumbu seksnya sedikit. Setelah dibaca lagi, pemahamannya sedikit beda. Memang ada unsur konspirasi, tapi tema utamanya lebih ke arah kisah seorang wanita yg menjadi duta besar.<br /><br />Plot:<br />Buku ini terbit di taun 80an, dimana Perang Dingin masih berlangsung antara Blok Barat dan Timur. Presiden terpilih Amerika, Paul Ellison, ingin mencoba menjalin hubungan baik dengan Rumania, salah satu negara Tirai Besi. Kalau berhasil, terbuka kemungkinan serupa untuk negara2 lainnya, dan mengurangi permusuhan antar Blok. Kebetulan dia punya satu calon yg menurutnya cocok untuk mengemban tugas sebagai Duta Besar Rumania, yaitu Mary Ashley. Seorang dosen ilmu politik dari kota kecil di Kansas City, yg memiliki pemahaman yg sama dengan Presiden tentang hubungan luar negeri.<br /><br />Presiden pun menawari Mary jabatan tersebut. Tawaran yang sangat terhormat, tapi ditolak oleh Mary, karena dia ingin tetap tinggal di sana bersama keluarganya. <br /><br />Hingga kemudian Edward, suaminya, terbunuh dalam suatu kecelakaan (alias dibuat seperti kecelakaan). Sehingga sudah tidak ada penghalang lagi untuk Mary meninggalkan kotanya, dan menerima tawaran sebagai duta besar ketika Stanton Rogers, penasehat utama Presiden mendatanginya. <br /><br />Mary pergi ke Washington bersama kedua anaknya, Beth dan Tim, dan menjalani training untuk menjadi duta besar. Dari sini Mary mulai mendapati kalau tidak semua orang senang dan setuju dengan penunjukannya, termasuk dari Departemen Luar Negeri. Selain itu, sebagai orang awam (non diplomat), banyak hal yang harus dipelajarinya, terkait menjalin kontak dengan perwakilan negara lain. Beberapa kali Mary melakukan kesalahan, tapi dia tidak patah semangat, dan semakin ingin membuktikan diri kalau dia bisa menjalankan tugasnya.<br /><br />Setelah beberapa bulan training, Mary dilantik dan kemudian dikirim ke Rumania. Dia langsung berhadapan dengan pekerjaan yang menumpuk, jadwal yang padat untuk kunjungan dan acara pesta antar kedutaan, dan mesti berurusan dengan Mike Slade, kepala staf kedutaannya yang menyebalkan. Juga menyaksikan sendiri kenyataan di Rumania, dimana segala sesuatu dipersulit.<br /><br />Sempat kagok di awal, Mary membuktikan diri sebagai duta besar yang cerdas dan mampu mengatasi masalah-masalah sulit, menorehkan beberapa prestasi penting. Bahkan dia menemukan cinta baru, pada diri Dr Louis Desforges dari kedutaan Prancis. Sayangnya, tidak semua berlangsung dengan manis. Dia menerima ancaman pembunuhan. Siapa gerangan yang hendak membunuhnya?<br /><br />Adalah sebuah sindikat internasional, Patriots for Freedom yang berisi orang2 penting dari berbagai negara, yang tidak menginginkan hubungan damai antara Blok Barat dan Blok Timur. Mereka mengadakan pertemuan2 rahasia, dan masing2 anggota punya kode nama tertentu. Merekalah yang turut mengatur kematian suami Mary, dan publikasi berlebihan pada Mary, supaya Mary menjadi image sempurna, untuk kemudian menghancurkannya, supaya tidak ada lagi usaha perdamaian di masa mendatang. <br /><br />Mereka menyewa seorang pembunuh andal bernama Angel, yang identitasnya tidak diketahui. Angel sebelumnya sudah menyebabkan kematian Marin Groza, tokoh oposisi Rumania yg sedang berlindung di Prancis, dan Ben Cohn, wartawan politik yang mencurigai motif penunjukan Mary. Dan sekarang Angel diutus untuk menghabisi Mary. <br /><br />Kepada siapa Mary mencari bantuan, sementara dia ragu apakah masih ada orang yang bisa dipercaya.<br /><br />-OOO-<br /><br />Sewaktu membaca pertama kali, terkesan ketika akhirnya identitas asli Angel terbuka. Kalo sekarang sih, karena sudah tau, jadinya mencocokkan situasi ketika Angel beraksi. Tapi Angel ini emang digambarkan superior, paham segala taktik untuk membunuh, dan kebanyakan caranya bukan membunuh langsung, tapi dengan masang alat/perangkap. <br /><br />Ada juga kekurangan menjelang akhir, dimana Sang Pengawas, si karakter bos musuh, melakukan kesalahan yang membocorkan identitasnya. Sepertinya ga konsisten dengan karakternya, yg harusnya cermat dan hati-hati.<br /><br />Bagian yang paling gw suka adalah ketika Mary menyelesaikan beberapa masalah dengan cerdik. Misalnya, dia mengusulkan pembentukan sister city antara Bucharest dengan Kansas ke Presiden Ionescu, sehingga Rumania membeli hasil pertanian Amerika. Atau ketika berhasil membebaskan seorang gadis Amerika yg ditahan di penjara Rumania.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17169427870266934058">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_409678250">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409678250" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3929792-vaultofbooks" class="left imgcol" title="VaultOfBooks"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1348989948p2/3929792.jpg" alt="VaultOfBooks" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/409678250?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3929792-vaultofbooks" class="user" title="VaultOfBooks">VaultOfBooks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119389.Windmills_of_the_Gods" title="Paperback 9780006174424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer409678250">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9129180050194217007">By Sidney Sheldon. Grade: B<br />It all began with an astounding call from the White House. One minute Mary Ashley, Kansas housewife and political science teacher, was chatting over dinner with her family; the next minute the President of the United States was asking her to become the new ambassador to Romania!<br />That call changes everything for Mary Ashley. She becomes an instant celebrity, hounded ‘by the press, courted by politicians. Finally Mary arrives in exotic Bucharest to take up her duties, con</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9129180050194217007">By Sidney Sheldon. Grade: B<br />It all began with an astounding call from the White House. One minute Mary Ashley, Kansas housewife and political science teacher, was chatting over dinner with her family; the next minute the President of the United States was asking her to become the new ambassador to Romania!<br />That call changes everything for Mary Ashley. She becomes an instant celebrity, hounded ‘by the press, courted by politicians. Finally Mary arrives in exotic Bucharest to take up her duties, confident, refreshingly candid-and dangerously innocent. For watching her closely is an in- visible network ‘of powerful men whose aim is to sabotage the President’s bold new peace plan. They are about to set a diabolical trap. And the inexperienced young diplomat is the perfect bait.<br /><br />The plot begins with the convening of the meeting of a secret council whose members vote for a certain resolution to be passed, which is diabolical, of course. The story then cuts to the presidential turmoil going on inside the White House. The President of United States, in an attempt to reconcile worldwide diplomatic relations, especially those with Romania, starts scouting potential candidates suitable to be appointed as the US Ambassador to Romania.<br />Enter Mary Ashley, the protagonist, who is nowhere on anybody’s radar. The daydreaming yet happily married, fiery yet composed typical Sidney Sheldon leading lady, Mary Ashley is a simple yet extraordinary political science teacher in Kansas when she receives a call from the President of United States asking her to consider the position of Romanian ambassador. Being of Romanian descent, it is almost as if her dreams had come true. But she turns down the offer for the simple reason that her family was not ready to move from the well-acquainted and accustomed life in Kansas to a completely alien country. Suddenly, peculiar as the timing is, Mary Ashley’s husband dies in a car accident under mysterious circumstances. With nothing left here, Mary Ashley takes up the job and is appointed as the United States Ambassador to Romania.<br />But it is never this simple. Somewhere in another part of the world, a secret plan is underway to scar this diplomatic arrangement and spoil the current presidency. An unwilling party to this grand conspiracy is the new ambassador, Mary Ashley. In her day-to-day working, she comes across various issues which needed attention. A disaster at first, Mary Ashley begins to learn the game of politics the hard way. In a game of hardened, seasoned veterans, Mary Ashley, just an amateur, tries to find an answer to the prevailing problems while dodging all attempts made on her life and family. How she does so – that is the question.<br />First and foremost, plotwise, this is unlike general Sidney Sheldon novels. Sidney Sheldon does not, in general, write plots pertaining to political conspiracies. But this is all that is different to WOTG. The strong, smart, lonely, heartbroken, twisted, independent leading lady, empowering circumstances, towering challenges in the wake of which the protagonist comes out as the unwilling and unexpected hero – all are pointed similarities in most of the Sidney Sheldon novels.<br />There were plenty of twists and turns in the plot. However, most of them were predictable. Nevertheless, the intricacies, for example, the assassination plot was commendable each and every time. The characters were very well sketched and assailants were well kept in the shadows.<br />All in all, another Sidney Sheldon light, enjoyable read but this time it’s not just a hand-in-the-cookie-jar, damsel-in-distress story.<br /><br /><br />Originally reviewed at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.vaultofbooks.com" target="_blank">www.vaultofbooks.com</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9129180050194217007">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_251123096">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251123096" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6771354-urszula" class="left imgcol" title="Urszula"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1319766771p2/6771354.jpg" alt="Urszula" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/251123096?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6771354-urszula" class="user" title="Urszula">Urszula</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6771354-urszula?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer251123096">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5117965418521199519">I like the action in this book. There is enough twist and turns to get the reader wondering who is the villain and who is the true hero.<br /><br />Normally I am not interested in politics, especially American. But since most of the action took place in Eastern Block country. I found the intrigues and manipulations quite interesting. I grew up in a communist country and could relate to the long lines at the shops, their overall lack of hope and bleakness. It brought back lots of unpleasant memories from my</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5117965418521199519">I like the action in this book. There is enough twist and turns to get the reader wondering who is the villain and who is the true hero.<br /><br />Normally I am not interested in politics, especially American. But since most of the action took place in Eastern Block country. I found the intrigues and manipulations quite interesting. I grew up in a communist country and could relate to the long lines at the shops, their overall lack of hope and bleakness. It brought back lots of unpleasant memories from my youth. <br /><br />It was great to see how a mother from a ‘normal’ town, became so involved in the conspiracy and danger. I like how she could face anything showing great courage and strength of character. I liked her journey and personal growth.<br /><br />And it was great to see that the real villain was a woman! How unusual and unexpected. I would have liked to see her captured and face the consequences of the actions.<br /><br />The epilogue lets you believe that the story continues... how unsettling!<br /><br />Overall I liked this book. It was a quick, pleasant read.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5117965418521199519">...more</a>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fBVVqQuZ6qUhQ1ftOwygfper0/QArI5vNPDuZusooR4ZwWp6+Uv+X62bI1ZFbUbM3lwQ7UlxycVe+ev0J71XWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P9e/F+LUohRnTKwDt0tNAsQ7meLE70D+PUQ2hqUDUwtaA4DEEAa27uuU2LjJKquwjcxa+40yB1RXTTMUaZalTg==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9068.Sidney_Sheldon">About Sidney Sheldon</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/9068.Sidney_Sheldon"><img alt="9068" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1209169297p2/9068.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5865062579299590625">Was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist. His TV works spanned a 20-year period during which he created I Dream of Jeannie (1965-70), Hart to Hart (1979-84), and The Patty Duke Show (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as Master of the Gam</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5865062579299590625">Was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist. His TV works spanned a 20-year period during which he created I Dream of Jeannie (1965-70), Hart to Hart (1979-84), and The Patty Duke Show (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as Master of the Game (1982), The Other Side of Midnight (1973) and Rage of Angels (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
